Being in Kolkata and missing Paramount means you are missing a slice of history of kolkata!! I have been to this place a number of times in college and school days.. and have been dearly missing the visits after being deployed to the rough and rude IT sector!! So just converted a 50-50 chance of being here to a 100% and landed up to this place in a November Saturday afternoon!!

Took a stroll in college streets.. took the smell of books.. smell of old days.. and entered Paramount.. the same unimpressive looks.. and I am happy that it did not get renovated in these couple of years!! Somehow I feel this old building charm adds to the 'juicy' experience here!!

I actually wanted to re-taste every single item on the menu.. but we three finally settled for one Coco-Malai, one Pineapple Malai and one Rose Malai.. Just forgot to mention not to put ice and that took away 0.5 points! The sherbets arrived in 5mins... Long glasses.. chocolaty, orangy and rosy.. top-filled with nuts and malai.. both spoon and straw provided to savour this specialty!! We jumped on the glasses with spoon... soft and smooth layer of kheer and generous amount of cashewnut, almonds and raisin filled in our mouth... as well as our senses.. The richness of the shake was somehow getting obstructed by the amount of ice put, but nevertheless the shake was as heavenly as it was 2-3years back.. 

It took us 5-6mins to finish our glasses... I was yet to taste the another favorite from this place.. Dab-malai.. but I was reminded about the lunch and had to leave that for my next visit!!

2013-08-25 19:46:52
Dr. Sandipan Ganguly
355958
4.5
I don't understand why they have the term juices, they make serbat and shakes, but i have never seen or drunk any juices there, neither I think they have one in their menu, only dab serbat is from coconut juice, but, they still mix rose water and other ingredients in it ( believe it? The recipe is from Acharya Prafulla Chandra Roy, amazing). What should I name of my favourite? Coco malai, pineapple, dab serbat, grapes crush, the very best green mango, and recently introduced tamarind. Sorry sirs, Passionfruit is not at per for the standard of your bar, this is a place of long long heritage and they make and break their own standard. Just don't try to compare them with anybody in the world. There are the places where you come to share original authentic and hall of the fame food and drink. I only can say, if you are a so called newcomer in college street, start your day with dalpuri and rajbhog from putiram, have grren mango from them, go and finish up your work. Have a pre lunch inside college square with ghugni, stew and pauruti. Have a grape crush and/or pineapple in there again, do some more work, have one of the best bengali authentic lunch with "macher matha diey pui shak, different fishes and oily, rich, yet so palatable pathar jhol with a big piece of alu (which will definitely make you forget about oh calcutta, 6 ballygunge place, kasturi, charnocks, bhajahari manna and all other so called big shots, and make you understand what real bengali cuisine is like) beside university hostel and opposite the mortuary, make your lunch digested by coming back to them and having a glass of dab serbet and "ek khili pan" from kalpataru. Finish up your work again and in between if you feel hot and thirsty, have a glass of "tetuler serber" and then a glass of coco malai as heavy snack. Finally finish up your day with bhetkir chop and mochar chop from "Kalika" and final glass of serbat from them, this time try lichhi, lemon or orange. Oh guys, One can die for it, when I go out of Kolkata for long, believe me, I simply miss these. No adjective is sufficient to describe the quality of any of the above, specially Paramount. Just try and be amazed. One of the best reason to stay in Kolkata.

4.5
There is a saying that if you happen to be in & around College Street / College Square and you haven't been to the Coffee House or at The Paramount Juice Centre , well then you probably belong to the unlucky few who missed a date with history of Kolkata! This is small outlet , very unimpressive though, but famous for its long list of eminent clients which includes legendaries like Sir Ashutosh Mukherjee , Bankim Chandra Chattopadhya , Satyajit Ray , eminent sportsmen . literateurs, cine stars & politicains including Ministers , Governors &  Judges , who have thronged this place for a glass full of magic in the form of Sherbets , Ghol & Juices which is very unique as well as mind boggling!The walls of the outlet takes  pride in  donning the cut-outs from newspaper clippings with rich reviews given by the greats of yester-years , reflecting its wonderful & glorious past!
I happened to visit this place way back one summer  in the late 70's accompanied by one of my school friend who had in fact insisted that we should drop in for a refreshing drink but would not tell me where! I had become restless as the scorching sun was taking a toll on my patience & just when I wasn't able to take it any more .........Lo here we were.....a small unimpressive & shabby looking place , till my eyes caught upon the clippings on the wall!
I swear in the name of the Lord that the Kacha Aamer Sherbet tasted like Ambrosia to me! I mean after the walk down the lane in the scorching sun there was nothing else that could have given you a feeling of utter satisfaction and the kind of pleasure which I derived   &  I could not help but ask for a second helping & thanked my dear  friend for having brought me  to a place which had a piece of history  attached to it!

P.S: I suggest if you do happen to in or around central kolkata / college street , please try it out for yourself &  then kindly revert to me regarding  your experience!Believe me , no one can match them, even though there are many reputed Juice houses in Kolkata, like the  Rallis etc of great importance but not as much as that of Paramount importance.!

After that day I have been there on umpteen occasions , with friends & office blokes & each time it has been an awesome experience!

From my college, Presidency University, Paramount is just a stone's throw away. Even though I've been going there for nearly a month now (I'm a Biological Sciences Major, 1st semester), I went to paramount only yesterday with a college friend who also happens to be a vociferous champion of Paramount. Given the utter negligence shown by popular hangout places like Cafe Coffee Day, KFC, McDonald's towards North Calcutta, me and my friends are now solely dependent on snooping out and experiencing less-heard-of eateries in and around College Street on a more-or-less regular basis. 
Thanks to zomato I had formulated a general conception of Paramount. So I had the quintessential Dub Sharbat. While waiting for our order, we enjoyed an invigorating conversation, free of any kind of interruptions. The parlour is small but is cozy rather that dingy. The interiors were a cool respite from the sweltering heat outside. From where we were sitting we could see a huge pile of dubs or raw coconut. We were thrilled to see the sharbat itelf. Arriving in a tall glass tumber, we could see for ourselves that the smoothie was wholly organic as it was really the colour of dub-water. Besides the straw for drinking, there was a spoon too for scooping out the generous portions of delicious nebulous dub-flesh. The cool effect of broken ice was accentuated by the marble-topped table. It was so refreshing that I'm still swooning from the delectable coolness. Forty rupees seems quite reasonable for this fantastic drink. I am proud to be the latest inductee of the Paramount Fan Club

North Kolkata has always been home to some of the most legendary places in the city. May it be the CU, Thanthania Kalibari, The Marble palace.... or the eateries.

When you come to the College Street area on a hot afternoon, u are bound to get thristy. But guess what, you are in luck!. Just hop in the Paramount Juice store just by the Pool side near the sanskrit collegiate. There are two things which make it better than all the Juice centres in the city:
1. Wide variety of Juices to choose from, some conventional, some not!
2. The taste is consitently great for all the flavours.

My personal favourite has been the Rose milk, very basic but amazingly delicious juice. Well the delicious word doesn't goes well with Juices, but after trying one of them from here u cant resist using it.


The low factor is that the space is very small and in rush u might need to hurry up for other people. But for foodies, who cares the space. There are no disputes of this being compared to any other Juice centre of the city, because this is the best of all. If you are in Kolkata, this place holds a tradition and a flagship of the signature Juices and flavours nature has allowed us to recognize. So please visit and it is gauranteed, you will come again and again!!! Happy Sipping!

2013-08-01 12:45:21
Anita Anand
1062261
4.5
A small sharbat parlour since 1918, with its original tables and chairs, it offers some delicious sherbats. I had two daaber sharbat (raw coconut) with ice and the cream of the daab, with a bit of sugar.  The owner is second generation and the next generation is there too. Started in the 1918 by his grandfather father, who came from east Bengal, the heavy weights of the 1930s and even those of the present day, patronised the Paramount. Its original name was Paradise, but his father renamed it. 

Its bustling with energy, a high turnover, very appropriate for all ages, and a welcome change form the heat of the outdoors.  A must visit.

2013-07-27 14:05:05
Kingshuk Bhattacharya
155296
4.5
Oh Paramount.. Even writing about you makes me thirsty! :( 

I really don't remember how many times I've been here, but enough to know quite a few facts about this place.. An important part of the history of this city, this place had once catered to the beautiful minds of our country.. From Rabindranath Tagore to Prafulla Chandra Roy, Narayan Gangopadhyay to Banaful, C V Raman to Amartya Sen, they've all been here.. Such a legacy, that it's been declared as 'Heritage Property' by Calcutta Municipal Corporation..

Bored? My apologies.. I'll quickly tell you why their Sherbets, not old glory, is the reason they are the best in Kolkata.. 

This place doesn't look anything out of ordinary.. But it does give you a homely vibe, a place where you can sit n relax, n feel comfortable enough.. The owner, Mr. Mazumder, personally comes and asks you what you want, n gives you some excellent suggestions too, if he thinks fit.. Definitely adds a personal touch to your whole experience..

Sherbets.. Where do I start? They have simple Syrups, Cream based and Curd based.. Try anything, anything you wish.. Their most famous is Dub Sherbet though.. Made of coconut water, they leave a  thick pulp on the top.. Oh my! It's refreshing, and wonderfully tasty.. Do make sure not to miss it if you're there..

I love their rose malai and coco malai too, but my personal favorite would be Grapes Crush.. I was really skeptical about trying it for the first time, but mr. Mazumder said they make it with a special grape syrup, which takes nearly 3-4 days for the fermentation.. And it was really a wonderful drink.. It has a rich, very rich texture, n it tastes beautiful.. Try it, n you'll know why it's one of the best sherbet place in Kolkata..

Do make it a point to visit this place.. You'll love this old charmer! :)

2013-07-18 20:17:18
Amarrtya Jana
993853
4.5
Paramount- A name that is synonymous with great sherbets and a name that has hosted some of the greatest persons to be born in Bengal. After a tiresome journey or a hectic day or just like that on a summer noon, the sherbets of this place have the capacity to cool and pacify even the most hot headed person on earth. I honestly feel they should start serving sherbets at Indian parliaments to help stop the altercations among matured people. Jokes apart, this place is the best if you want to have good quality sherbets at a very moderate price. I am not aware of any other place in Kolkata serving better sherbets at a price range even remotely close to Paramount's.

Located in college street, this very small establishment is famous among college students, primarily because college street is the place where we head for books at discounted prices. Even then I would suggest everyone who has a taste for sherbets to visit this place for some pleasant and cool stuffs.

Coming to the ambiance. Its simply not good. Paramount is a shop serving their great preparations in a hilariously small room which at times becomes very congested. The table tops are made of marble, and they have benches, like we used to have in school, instead of proper chairs. Certain things in the shop are bound to attract your eyes. One is a list of famous people who have been to this place and the other is a head of a deer which was told to me to be real. Being an establishment of nearly a century this place has hosted freedom fighters like Netaji to celebrities like Uttam Kumar. It also boasts several newspaper articles that have been put on the wall to make new customers showcase its prestige. The sherbets are served in those standard tall glasses used by hawkers on a roadside. But the service is quiet fast. The person,who seems to be the owner is very prompt in his actions and most of the times the sherbets are served by him. The kitchen is at the rear end of the shop, hidden from the customer's view just by means of a curtain. So nothing appealing about the ambiance.

What makes paramount a place worth visiting are their brilliantly prepared sherbets and their heritage status. Most of the standard sherbets, priced at 30 rupees are curd based. They come in various flavors like rose, green mango, pineapple, banana and others. The curd base is the cardinal difference between this place and others that are similar. I, being a regular to this place have tasted most of their sherbets and each one of them proved to be awesome. Not very sweet, nor very mild, the sherbets bear the stamp of originality. They also have a topping of malai on every glass of their sherbets. If you want something uniquely different then go for their coco- malai or the dab sherbet. The dab sherbet is indeed a treat and is sure to impress everyone. It is a sherbet made with coconut water that is refreshing in its taste. Most people avoid the banana sherbet and I used to fall in the same category. But once a person in the shop recommended it to me. I was told that the banana syrup is the costliest and the best in taste and truly it turned out to be the best among the ones priced at 30 bucks. However I tend not to stop at just one glass, every time I visit this place and end up ordering at least two different flavors. I would recommend this place to every one. The old school sherbets of this place can never be substituted by any cold drinks. 

As I end my review with a 4.5/5 for this place I would request everyone to indulge yourselves in the classy taste of Paramount's sherbet and witness the fact "OLD IS GOLD".

2013-06-21 23:23:46
Mukulita Ganguly
207896
4.0
After roaming about for hours in College Street, buying books, we four (very tired souls)
unanimously decided that we had to end our hectic day with something cool and soothing from Paramount. It is located opposite to the College Square Swimming Club.
We were warmly greeted by a friendly and elderly person, whose ancestors had served great personalities like Rabindranath Tagore, Satyajit Ray, Uttam Kumar and so many others. He arrived at our table and gave us some helpful suggestions about choosing our drink. Keeping his suggestions in mind, a glass of cocoa malai, daab sherbet, crushed grapes and litchi syrup was ordered. Thanks to the prompt service, our drinks arrived in 5 minutes. All the concoctions (garnished with a layer of crushed ice) are so unique and awesome in their own way, it is hard to choose one over the other. If you want something light and subtle, then go for the daab sherbet which is made with coconut water topped with coconut malai. The cocoa malai is a milk based drink with clotted cream, chocolate, crushed nuts and raisins. The litchi drink is very fresh and full of flavour. The most interesting drink is the crushed grapes which is slightly wine flavoured. This red coloured drink is the healthiest one in the list, which also acts as an Ayurvedic medicine.
I must say, along with our fulfilling glass of sherbets we got to know a lot about this
historically significant, pleasant little parlour set up in 1918. It felt great, knowing that the
idea of daab sherbet had first originated from the great Acharya Prafulla Chandra Roy's
mind.
If there is anyone who has not yet stepped into this place even for once, please make it a
point to visit this sherbet lover's paradise. The malai and daab sherbet are the most
renowned ones, but you can have anything and you won't be disappointed. Apart from the above ones, I would recommend the kesar and vanilla malai sherbet and green mango syrup.
While leaving, we (four satisfied and happy souls) got to know that this place will celebrate it's 100th anniversary after 5 years. Goes without saying, we would love to be there again and again!
P.S : Check out their menu card! :)

2013-06-11 16:12:31
Bhavesh Bhatia
199538
3.0
A restaurant of paramount importance in College Street
3 out of 5

Situated amidst the busy area of College Street, Paramount is one of the popular destinations in the city that has retained its heritage, culture and standard since it opened in 1918.
Nowadays, I have heard a lot of criticism about this place from many people, but my honest advice is - don't judge this place by its appearance while comparing this place with other juice and syrup parlours that have cropped up in the city in recent years. Just go in and try to feel the heritage and value of this place before you draw any conclusions. 

The ambience is really very ordinary and unappealing as are the waiters. But they are very humble and polite and serve every customer in a homely fashion (without any exaggeration). Their menu only includes a variety of syrups, juices and shakes, and there's nothing more blissful than a glass of cold and refreshing drink on a hot summer day. Among their various juices, I personally prefer their Kacha Aamer Sarbot and Daaber Sarbot. But for a change, I always love to try their Rose Syrup and Mango Shake. Other fruity ones are also very nice but as I am not very fond of fruity flavors, I generally prefer to stick to these. Another item which is really mentioned worthy is their lassi (really a refreshing option for hot summer days!). 

This small family run business can easily go in for some modernization by including some more snacks or baked goods, but what I like the most is that they prefer to retain that traditional pride in their way of doing business rather than chasing modernization like other establishments. Probably this unique feature still gives this 'paramount' syrup parlour a number one ranking. Moreover, this place charges very reasonably for their beverages which are prepared and served with a lot of love and care.

2013-03-23 12:03:23
Manjari Chowdhury
285678
3.5
A part of Calcutta's heritage this Sherbet center ( I prefer using the term sherbet because they do not serve fresh fruit juices but drinks made from fruits etc) is even more special due to its special location at 'boi-para' (the neighbourhood of books) Long before Flipkart and Uread.Com had even been invented book-lovers would throng the streets of College Street for books on any subject under the sun. Students would get a good bargain on their favourite novels and books of interest. Even today it is still a paradise for book-lovers and students. This place is mainly thronged by students from the nearby University of Calcutta and the prestigious Presidency college. Located opposite to College Square where swimmers plash around to cool off the not so lucky ones come here to cool down with their cooling drinks. Considering the fact that they use flavourings for most of the drinks it might not be a wise decision to travel all the way for the taste of the drinks but visiting it for its heritage is worth the effort because this opened its gates in 1918 and from my research it seems that it was a regular meeting place for revolutionaries  whose efforts gave us an independent nation. They have a list of famous personalities who have graced the shop hanging from the neatly painted walls.  Due to the sultry weather I opted for the famous Dab-Sherbet with crushed ice ( tender coconut water mixed with sugar and rose flavouring if I am not mistaken) It is a perfect cooler for Calcutta's humid ,unbearable heat. They charge an extra Rs2 if ice is not added since that requires a greater amount of tender coconut water to be used. A word of caution: In case you like your creamy drinks on the lighter side of sweetness ask them to add very little sugar because my aunt's green mango flavoured creamy drink was a bit too sweet for those who like mild sweetness. When visiting the area it is a must visit for anyone to cool down for a while during the summers. They get extra points for the cleanliness of the place.                    I personally did not like the arrangement of sitting because the benches where one sits has no back rest and due to the lack of space you often  bump against someone's back sitting back to back with you.

This is a family run place and u can see the warmth here and the pride they take in their product... the menu is not too vast but every drink is prepared with a lot of love and care.

This place may be small,but it sure packs a punch.The first thing that hits you is the old calcutta charm this dandy old place has.Its been graced by the presence of many bengali celebrities of the 80's and 90's...And it still lives upto its legendary reputation..Tucked away in the College street area of north calcutta,this place is an awesome watering hole for the parched souls all around.Ive tried out almost all their juice and sherbet offerings.Some of their more popular ones include Daab Sherbet and Coco malai..but even their simple orange and green mango and lemon flavored curd based drinks are refreshingly good. Almost all their drinks contain crushed ice;in fact it costs extra if you have one without ice. Visit this place in summer,and let this age old place help you beat the heat.

2012-11-08 21:04:13
Esha Banerjee
79129
4.0
This place is purely old school calcutta..its a very small establishment with a very limited crammed seating arrangement for roughly 20 people(and when you are with friends you can always squueze in some more folks).
The ambience consists of the chatter of the customers,of the people who take and also serve the orders.Its a favourite of the college goers,the book-hunters,the university employees and the people who came back here year after after year to relive the old memories..
The place serves malai sherbets,sodas,syrups.Though most of the items on offer are great,the dab sherbet is the signature item of the place.My personal recommendation would be a green mango,you can also try rose or vanilla malai,the coco malai is a bit heavier and filling,and the more adventerous can try the grapes crush.All the drinks come with crushed ice,and they charge extra if you do not want ice.
A excellent visit on a hot summer afternoon!
